COLOMBIA
THIRD NATIONAL ROADS SECTOR PROJECT
Outline of Terms of Reference-for Technical AssistAnce for MOPT
in Road Maintenance ManageMent
Background
1.       MOPT's maintenance expenditures per km of road are very high (about
US$3,000/km), but operational efficiency remains low because of weak planning,
diversion of maintenance funds to major emergency works and lack of adequate
information and costing systems. In the early 80s, consultants put in place a
management system and assisted MOPT in the creation and operation of a new
maintenance coordinating unit (GAM, Grupo de Anovo Al Mantenimiento) at the
central plant. The system mainly focused on maintenance cost accounting. It
was implemented in four districts under Loan 1471-CO, but MOPT was unable to
expand it to the remaining districts under Loan 2121-CO. A periodic
maintenance program was introduced in 1982 to be executed by contract, but it
partially failed because of inadequate supervision procedures and the
contractors' tendency to carry out only high-unit-cost work items and neglect
others. However, in 1986 MOPT launched a program contracting basic routine
maintenance with labor-absorbing small cooperatives (micrQemogesas) of 12 to
15 workers, each covering about 50 km of road. This innovative initiative
proved to be a cost-effective alternative to the force account operations. By
1990 the microemoresas program included 333 cooperatives covering over 17900
km, about 70 % of the national road network. MOPT also made some efforts to
improve spare parts management by implementing computerized inventories in
some dLstricts. During the preparation of the Third National Roads Sector
Project, MOPT formulated the annual maintenance plan and performance budgets
for 1992-95, based on the actual maintenance needs reported by the districts;
the formulation of such plans proved difficult due to the lack of a well-
established systematic planning procedure. Furthermore, there still is a need
to strengthen other areas such as maintenance control and supervision as well
as the coordination between different units involved in road maintenance at
both the central and district level.
Objectives
2.       The Technical Assistance aims at developing a comprehensive highway
maintenance management system and assisting MOPT in its implementation in MOPT
headquarters and the districts. The technical assistance will strengthen
MOPT's ability to:
a) establish a sound maintenance policy optimizing the use of cost-
effective external entities like Microempresas and larger contractors;



- 136 -
ANNEX 7
Attachment .
Page 2 of 8
b) prepare multi-annual maintenance programs and performance budgets, thus
improving the allocation of funds and resources;
c) schedule, carry out and control the maintenance works within an annual
plan managing maintenance resources efficiently;
d) operate all workshop facilities adequately and maintain MOPT's road
maintenance equipment fleet properly; and,
e) monitor maintenance operational costs and other maintenance related
expenditures, providing the necessary interface with the government
budgetary system.
ScoRe of the Assistance
3.       The consultants hired under this technical assistance will perform
the following main tasks:
a) reviewing current maintenance procedures, policies and organizational
capabilities within MOPT and the districts;
b) upgrading the Road Maintenance Inventory, organized on the basis of
homogeneous road segments;
c) defining performance criteria and standards for maintenance activities,
adjusted to regional variations;
d) implementing a comprehensive maintenance management system to
effectively plan, schedule, execute and/or control maintenance works
carried out by force account, microemoresas and large contractors,
assisted by automatization at both central and district levels;
e) implementing a comprehensive equipment management system, directed to
establishing equipment operating costs, evaluating equipment maintenance
policies and procedures, and managing inventories of spare parts;
f) setting up cost accounting procedures to support the maintenance and
equipment management systems;
g) implementing reporting procedures, designed to provide timely, useful
and accurate information;
h) establishing an effective maintenance policy, tailored to the local
existing conditions and constraints;
i) formulating a three-year road maintenance program and performance
budget, coordinated with other highway investments (construction and
rehabilitation); and,
j) training MOPT's maintenance personnel.
4.       As part of the Government's decentralization policy, MOPT plans to
gradually transfer to the departments the maintenance and construction
responsibilities over a portion of its national road network. Therefore, the
road maintenance and equipment management systems should be developed taking
into account this situation, ensuring they can efficiently handle the changes
that this policy will introduce in the road network and maintenance resources,
and they are suitable for their transference to the departmental agencies.



- 137 -
ANNEX 7
Attachment 1
Page 3 of 8
5.       Reviewing current maintenance procedures. policies and organizational
capabilities within MOPT and the districts. The technical assistance will
review the current procedures and policies used by MOPT in order to assess
their efficiency and scope in relation to the whole cycle of maintenance
management: planning; organizing and programming; executing and controlling;
and evaluating maintenance results. By this means, the consultants will point
out deficiencies in both technical and organizational matters, mechanisms to
overcame such deficiencies and sequence in which these mechanisms should be
implemented according to their relevance for the system development.
Accordingly, the technical assistance will define a system development action
plan, which will facilitate assigning counterpart staff to work in the
different areas.
6.       URaradina the Road Maintenance Inventorv.  The technical assistance
will review the scope and consistency of the information available through the
Road Maintenance Inventory as well as the efficiency and reliability of the
data collection procedures, and will search for other related sources of
information existing within MOPT. Taking into account the Road Maintenance
Inventory data, organizational limits, construction data, traffic and
environment, the technical assistance will divide the road network into
homogeneous segments, appropriate for maintenance management purposes; a code
will be assigned to each road segment to facilitate its identification in the
system. After this analysis, the consultants will propose an upgraded system
to collect, handle and analyze all the data needed in order to ensure that the
Road Maintenance Inventory has the capabilities to: i) establish road network
condition and maintenance needs; ii) point out road segments with high
deterioration rates; iii) provide a list of candidate road segments for
rehabilitation works; and iv) provide 'he basic information to appraise the
impact of maintenance policies and programs. In addition, the consultants
will implement, in MOPT central office and in each district, an emergency site
inventory sub-system, linked to the road maintenance inventory and designed to
improve emergency operations efficiency by keeping record of the occurrence of
slope stability related problems (location, magnitude, consequences for road
traffic and measures undertaken to correct and/or prevent their recurrence)
and establishing priorities and cost-effective solutions for site improvement.
The technical assistance will lead MOPT staff in updating the Road Maintenance
Inventory and implementing the new procedures.
7.       Defining performance criteria and standards for maintenance
activities. The technical assistance will revise maintenance activities,
maintenance performance standards, quantity standards and unit costs used by
MOPT to prepare performance budgets. The definition of these elements should
provide a common basis of comparison of program compliance, unit costs,
resource usage, productivity and other management and technical indicators,
taking into account regional variations (climate, remoteness from base
resources) and differences inherent in alternative modes of maintenance (by
microemoresas, force account, contract or combinations of the preceding),
which could impact on productivity, cost, crew size and equipment
requirements. The performance standards will include appropriate performance



- 138 -
ANNEX 7
Attachment 1
Page 4 of 8
criteria, providing information on the level-of-service to be provided,
recommended months that the activity is to be performed and how often is
carried out, quality standards for the tasks involved, and scheduling
requirements to coordinate with other work activities. The quantity standards
will take into account road categories and conditions as well as the level-of-
service to be provided according to a selected maintenance policy; as the
latter may change due to budget constrains, the technical assistance will
prepare practical guidelines to match quantity standards and maintenance
levels at the planning phase and to carry out the selected maintenance policy
at the executing phase. The technical assistance will set up guidelines for
unit cost analysis capable of taking into account the above-mentioned factors
and comparing cost-efficiency among the possible alternative modes to carry
out each activity to facilitate decisions on contracting. These guidelines
will also provide for the necessary feedback from the maintenance evaluation
phase on actual costs and performance of the activities carried out within the
program.
8.       Implementing a comprehensive maintenance management system.  The
technical assistance will set up a rational methodology for road maintenance
management, comprising: i) planning multi-annual maintenance plans and
performance annual budgets , classified into routine, periodic and emergency
programs to be carried out by force account, microempresas and large
contractors; ii) organizing and programming maintenance works at the district
level, scheduled in an annual work calendar to match best technical
performance criteria and work load levelling; iii) executing maintenance
activities under the force account program and supervising maintenance works
performed by microemoresas and large contractors; and iv) avaluating
maintenance results, based on the adherence to the annual work plan, annual
budget and maintenance performance standards, and evolution of the network
condition. The system will be implemented at both the central and district
level. Modular automatization will facilitate the data analysis and reporting
required in the different phases of maintenance management at both the central
and district level; consequently, the computerized system will comprise
various sub-systems, involving the creation of several data base files and the
development of programs to manage these files, analyze data and prepare
reports, in a user-friendly-menu-driven software. In order to formulate
multi-annual maintenance plans adjusted to current and future maintenance
needs, the system will make use of analytical models to predict road
deterioration under selected maintenance policies as well as procedures to
coordinate the maintenance programs with other highway investments, such as
road construction and rehabilitation, which could modify the road network
under maintenance during a certain time period. The system will strengthen
the district's ability to develop and monitor weekly or bi-weekly programs
tailored to reflect work priorities, the availability of maintenance resources
(personnel, equipment and materials) and special conditions (urgent or
emergency situations). The consultants will also review and upgrade the
procedures to contract and supervise the maintenance services provided by
either microemgresas or large contractors.



- 139 -
ANNEX 7
Attachment I
Page S of 8
9.       Implementing a comprehensive eauipment management system.  The
technical assistance will collect and analyze the data on the availability and
use of MOPT's equipment fleet and will review the Sub-Directorate of
Equipment's programs and policies on equipment management. After that, the
consultants will put in place a comprehensive equipment management system
capable of evaluating equipment operating costs, equipment preventive
maintenance policies and procedures, and managing stocks and inventories of
spare parts. The system will comprise several sub-systems to allow a modular
or phased implementation, but sharing some data bases to reduce data
collection and reporting from the field. The technical assistance will
implement: i) a computerized equipment master inventory to record changes in
equipment assignments and keep track of equipment unit's history for the
lifetime of each unit; ii) a computerized equipment maintenance and operation
cost sub-system to collect and/or calculate equipment ownership, maintenance,
operation and administrative costs, charge these costs to each unit in the
inventory and generate the analytical reports required by equipment managers
at all levels for the development of equipment maintenance labor standards,
equipment replacement planning, preventive maintenance scheduling and analyses
of equipment maintenance and rehabilitation programs; iii) a computerized
parts and materials inventory sub-system to maintain a file of all parts
stocked in the workshop facilities together with balances on hand in each
facility in order to analyze parts usage, generate stock management
information and process accounting transactions for parts issued, receLpts,
and adjustments; and iv) manual shop work-in-process control procedures, to
control scheduled repairs and inspections, non-scheduled maintenance and
repair backlogs. The consultants will review current MOPT's policies for
equipment acquisition, assignment and disposal, and will recommend the
policies and procedures to be followed in the future.
10.      Settina uo cost accounting orocedures.  The technical assistance will
set up a cost accounting system to support the cost collection and analysis
systems developed for road maintenance and equLpment management purposes. This
system will aim at: i) introducing reliable procedures to monitor MOPT's
payments and expenditures according to work progress; Li) developing and
charging equipment rental rates and reporting actual equipment cost
performance against the planned budgets; and iii) providing the necessary
interface between the existing budgetary system and the maintenance and
equipment management systems to enable the reconciliation of costs and
resource usage.
11.      Implementina reportina procedures.  The technical assistance will
give special attention to the implementation of a reporting sub-system capable
of providing timely, useful and accurate information at the required level.
Work orders and weekly crew work report will indicate not only the type and
amount of work done but also accurately identify the resources used and the
road segment where works were carried out; their design will provide for easy
use in the field. The burden of data reporting will be reduced by limiting
manual data collection to field operations and implementing the computerized
system to generate the management evaluation reports, such as monthly

maintenance activities reports, district monthly work progress and cost
summary reports, and monthly/quarterly/annual work progress and cost report.
12.      Establishina an effective maintenance Dolicy.  The consultants will
analyze existing local conditions affecting maintenance planning, such as
resource constraints, in-house and external absorptive capacity, regional
developing plans, traffic levels and road network condition, and will define
alternative policies to carry out road maintenance, representing different
maintenance levels and approaches. By means of an economic and impact
analysis involving network modeling through representative road segments, the
technical assistance will assess the most effective(s) maintenance policy(ies)
for the short and long term, tailored to the local existing conditions and
constraints. The recommended policy(ies), which will guide the formulation of
the future road maintenance programs, will be defined in terms of: policy
goals; budgeting and resource requirements; maintenance of quality standards
on the road network during the implementation period; priorities in work
execution; type and frequency of maintenance works to be performed by force
account, microempresas and larger contractors in representative road segments
within each district. The technical assistance will develop guidelines to
interpret and carry out the policy's recommendations through the maintenance
management process.
13.      Formulatincr a three-year road maintenance Droaram.  The technical
assistance will formulate the road maintenance program and performance budget
for the period 1993-1995, developed along lines set up by the policies and
procedures introduced through the maintenance management system. These
maintenance programs will be prepared considering routine, periodic and
emergency maintenance, starting with the needs of the districts and deriving
the national program as a sum of the programs of the 26 districts. The
programs will seek optimum use of the external maintenance capacity within
each district when defining those components to be carried out either by
microemDresas or large contractors; the consultants will choose the work to be
contracted, prepare bidding documents for the procurement of contractor
services and group these works in lots of attractive size for local
contractors taking account of their equipment and working capital. The
consultants will prepare all the documents needed to support and implement
these programs both at the central level and the districts. They will also
assist MOPT in preparing the appropriate documents for government approval,
providing information on the scope and goals of the proposed maintenance
plans, on the work program impact on the network and on the consequences of
any eventual reduction in the maintenance budget.
14.      Trainina MOPT maintenance personnel.  The consultants will train the
personnel directly involved in maintenance activities. They will provide on-
the-job training to the counterpart personnel assigned by MOPT, making them
effectively participate in all technical assistance activities to ensure full

The technical assistance will prepare and carry out a maintenance training
program for technical and administrative personnel involved in maintenance

COLOMBIA
THIRD NATIONAL ROADS SECTOR PROJECT
Outline of Terms of Reference for Technical Assistance for MOPT
in Standards gor Structural Pavement Desian and Road Rehabilitation
Backqround
1.       MOPT contracts most of the engineering studies for new roads with
local consultants. Road rehabilitation studies are initially prepared by
MOPT's district engineers, providing a basic estimation of activities and
quantities required; consultants hired for construction supervision review
such estimates and complete the studies. The lack of appropriate standards
for structural pavement design has been one of the factors that hampered
MOPT's capacity to provide sound and consistent pavement designs throughout
the road network in accordance with prevailing conditions, and avoid
successive design changes during project construction. Variations in the
quality of the studies and in the criteria applied by the designers very often
lead to pavement structures that are poorly related to the design parameters
(traffic, materials sources and drainage conditions) and are not cost-
effective. The Sub-Directorate of Projects assigns staff engineers to
supervise the preparation of the engineering studies, but the lack of broadly
accepted design procedures and a list of the items that should be included in
each study, as well as the scope of such items, has made it difficult for the
supervisor to address project deficiencies.
Obiectives
2.       The technical assistance aims at implementing uniform standards for
structural design of new pavements and rehabilitation of existing pavements,
through the development of a Pavement Catalogue or a comprehensive but
practical Pavement Design Guide to be broadly used by consultants and MOPT
technicians in all engineering studies. The standards will improve the
quality of these studies and strengthen MOPT's capacity to:
a) produce cost-effective and consistent pavement designs reflecting
existing local conditions and road management policies;
b) reduce the need for changes in pavement design during the construction
stage; and
c) monitor pavement performance and plan timely road maintenance and
rehabilitation activities.



- 144 -
ANNEX 7
Attachment 2
Page 2 of 5
ScoRe of the Assistance
3.       The consultant will guide MOPT's task force and will coordinate on-
going research activities with other agencies involved in pavement research in
the country. The main tasks to be carried out by this consultant will include
the following:
a) establishing a general framework and work methodology to be followed by
the task force;
b) defining the inputs and models required to analyze pavement performance
in existing local conditions;
c) reviewing and upgrading existing procedures to evaluate mechanical
properties of soils and road materials in engineering studies;
d) assessing research needs to improve or validate the design procedures or
tq promote new technologies;
e) upgrading the guidelines for pavement design studies;
f) reviewing supporting documents prepared by the task force and preparing
the final reports; and
g) assisting MOPT in the implementation of the procedures and standards
developed by the task force.
4.      Establishinq a ceneral framework and work methodoloav for the task
force. The consultant will review the criteria and guidelines used by MOPT
engineers and local consultants for the structural design of pavements as well
as the consistency and quality of the final designs, by comparing design
parameters and performance predictions with construction and actual
performance data of typical in-service highways throughout the road network.
This review will cover both the design of new pavements and the rehabilitation
of existing ones and will require field visits to on-going construction
projects as well as in-service roads. In this phase the consultant will also
discuss the different pavement design approaches used by other road
administration agencies, such as standard pavement structures (Pavement
Catalogues), analytical-empirical and mechanistic-empirical methods (including
performance models), analyzing the advantages and disadvantages of each one
taking into account the existing local conditions.  After this analysis the
consultant will: i) recommend the methodology to be used by MOPT; ii) define
additional data needs and the procedures to collect and analyze such data;
iii) coordinate data collection and research efforts to be performed by MOPT
staff according to the agreed design approach.
5.       Defining inDuts and models recuired to analyze Davement performance.
The consultant will define the pavement design parameters and the best
procedures to study them under the selected design approach, taking into
account existing local conditions and laboratory facilities. Subsequently,
the technical assistance will set up comprehensive procedures to: i) evaluate
the damage factors of traffic loads and estimate the future number of axle
load repetitions expected during the pavement design life, using basic
information provided by existing (or upgraded if necessary) traffic counting
procedures; ii) evaluate the seasonal variations in road material properties



- 145 -
ANNEX 7
Attachment 2
Page 3 of 5
induced by changes in environmental conditions throughout the year, dividing
the country into regions according to environmental factors which affect
pavement performance and translating climatic and other environmental data
into typical design parameters and specific design requirements for each
region; iii) establish the effective bearing capacity of the subgrade soil,
using existing (or upgraded if necessary) laboratory tests and/or appropriate
correlations with standard tests; iv) typify the mechanical properties of
local materials and mixes such as asphalt concrete and cement concrete mixes,
using existing (or upgraded if necessary) laboratory tests and relating these
test results to the design process; v) assess the strength parameters of the
pavement layers and foundation from non-destructive testing techniques, using
the equipment locally available for pavement evaluation; vi) assess drainage
conditions and techniques to study problems related to the presence of water
in pavement structures; and vii) identify the different alternativ' solutions
available through technologies which have proved to be cost-effective and also
feasible to implement. In order to develop the standards for structural
pavement design, the consultant will implement the analytical and mechanistic
models needed to analyze the behavior and performance of pavement structures
under typical situations, training MOPT task force in the use of such
analytical tools. Different methodologies will be outlined for flexible,
rigid and semi-rigid pavements as well as for the design of new pavements and
the rehabilitation of existing ones.
6.       Uqarading existine procedures to evaluate mechanical Prooerties of
soils and road materials in enaineerino studies. The technical assistance
will compare design and performance data from existing pavement structures
with the recommendations derived from the application of the accepted methods
for pavement design to similar conditions. During this developing phase, the
assessment of soil mechanical properties will be based on the most rational
testing techniques, like the resilient modulus or others, depending on the
availability within the country of the appropriate testing device for research
purposes. However, for standards implementation, the technical assistance
will upgrade the existing soil and road materials evaluation procedures
introducing better field sampling and laboratory practices, but still
supported by testing equipment currently available in local laboratories. The
consultant will recommend on best practices for both pavement design and
construction regarding the treatment of special soil conditions, such as
volcanic and collapsible soils found in the Cordillera Central, and laterite
and expansive soils.
7.       Assessino research needs.  The consultant will identify the  priority
research needs in the fields of pavement design and rehabilitation to improve
or validate the design procedures and to promote the use of new technologies.
The technical assistance will delineate an action plan to carry out those
research activities required in the short run to develop the standards. The
consultant will assist MOPT and other agencies eventually involved in such
activities by providing the necessary guidance.

8.       Unoradina the uuidelines for pavement desictn studieL.   The consultant

account the changes in pavement design procedures and improved practices
developed. These guidelines will vary according to the purpose of the study,
such as the design of a new facility or the rehabilitation of an existing one,

technicians and local consultants.
Staffing

COLOMBIA
THIRD NATIONAL ROADS SECTOR PROJECT
Outline of Terms of Reference for Technical Assistance for MOPT
in the Suoervision of Road Construction Works
Backaround
1.       The supervision of road construction works in Colombia is mainly
performed by local consultants and MOPT's district engineers are assigned to
monitor the contracts for both construction and work supervision.
Construction practices are very often affected by the difficult topographical
conditions. However, there are several areas where supervision can be
improved. Frequent deficiencies in the engineering studies have contributed
in the past to shifting supervisor's attention from quality control activities
to the design of missing project components, contract administration and work
re-scheduling to match it to budget allocations. The Guidelines for
Supervisors (Directrices para Interventores), a guideline of supervision
activities, lacks particulars on quality assurance. In addition, some
technical specifications are outdated and others do not define with enough
detail the quality standards for work approval, giving more room to
misinterpretation during construction. In spite of several positive measures
introduced by MOPT, supervision costs are still too high in relation to
project costs and need to be reduced.
Qbiectives
2.       The Technical Assistance aims at strengthening MOPT's technical
capabilities tc more effectively program and supervise road construction works
carried out by contractors and supervision tasks performed by consultants or
MOPT engineers. The objectives of the technical assistance are:
a) to address the main constraints preventing the supervisors from assuming
a more effective role in the supervision of construction works;
b) to enhance the quality of construction work and the cost-effectiveness
of supervision activities; and
c) to improve the allocation of funds and resources to work construction,
through more efficient project schedulinq and monitoring practices;
Scone of the Assistance
3.       The consultant will perform the following main tasks:
a) assessing and reporting main deficiencies in construction monitoring and
technical supervision;
b) reviewing the existing supervision procedures;



- 149 -
ANNEX 7
Attachment_3
Page 2 of 4
c) developing guidelines to improve construction supervision and project
monitoring;
d) developing a comprehensive construction cost estimate manual;
e) assisting MOPT's task force in the preparation of the new technical
specifications;
f) assessing training needs among private supervisors and contractors to
ensure a smooth transition to new procedures and specifications; and
g) providing on-the-job training to MOPT's staff.
4.       Assessing and reporting main deficiencies in construction, monitorinq
and technical supervision. The consultant will visit several projects under
construction. During these visits the consultant will analyze: i) contractors
performance and compliance with the technical specifications; ii) supervision
facilities, organization and personnel skills, with special attention to the
supervisor's capacity to carry ous and interpret field and laboratory tests;
iii) timeliness and reliability of the quality control activities performed by
the supervisor; iv) criteria for work scheduling; and v) suitability of work
reporting procedures. In each visit, the consultant will prepare a guideline
addressing the deficiencies observed. The consultant will also report to the
sub-directorate of supervision on the main findings resulted from each visit;
these short back-to-office -reports will help the technical assistance to
develop upgraded procedures, tailored to actual conditions and needs.
5.       Reviewing existina supervision procedures.  The consultant will
review MOPT supervision procedures, including the Guidelines for Supervisors,
typical monthly supervision reports, contract monitoring practices and data
needed by MOPT's budget monitoring computerized system. After this review,
and taking into account the experience gained through the field visits, the
consultant will: i) address the main constraints preventing the local
supervisors from assuming a more effective role in the supervision of
construction works; ii) identify the measures to upgrade MOPT supervision
practices; and iii) prepare an action plan to implement such measures.
6.       Develonina cuidelines to improve construction supervision and oroiect
monitorina. The technical assistance will upgrade the Guidelines for
Supervisors, introducing improved practices in the fields of: composition of
supervision teams, job descriptions and personnel skills; work organization
and basic facilities; programming of construction work and supervision
activities; quality control; work progress reporting; contract administration
and accountability in the decision raking process. Such practices will aim at
improving the quality of construction work and the cost-effectiveness of
supervision activities, particularly in projects with lengthy construction
time. The monthly supervision reports will be upgraded to include more
relevant information in order to assess work progress and quality, and
expedite project monitoring. The terms of reference for contracting
supervision services will also be updated, according to the changes introduced
in the supervision practices. The consultant will also assist MOPT in
upgrading its project monitoring capabilities, implementing a computerized
system to: i) store and manage relevant data on work progress, project

expenditures, budget allocations, contract modifications and contractors
performance; ii) analyze the data and generate the necessary reports for

7.       pevelooing a comRrehensive construction cost estimate manual.  The
consultant will review the procedures used by MOPT and local consultants to
estimate construction costs and cost escalation. The technical assistance

MOPT's district supervisors will also participate in such visits.

COLOMBIA
Third National Roads Sector Project
Outline of Terms of Reference for the
Study for the Decentralization of Manaaement of National Road Network
Background
1.          The Government has embarked on a series of reforms designed to
modernize transportation operations through effective integration of all modes
of transport, adjustment of the institutional framework and efficient
utilization of resources. The Study for the Restructuring of the Public Works
and Transportation Sector, currently in preparation under the supervision of
the DNP, provides a framework for the restructuring of the management,
planning, coordination and control functions in the transportation sector, and
the reorganization of execution of public works on a nationwide basis. This
is to be complemented by the redistribution of responsibilities for the
construction and maintenance of transportation infrastructure among the
national government, the Departments and the municipalities, according to the
principle of decentralization endorsed by the Government and the new
Constitution. The proposed study responds to the need to transfer to the
Departments part of the national road network and corresponding financial
resources managed by the Ministry of Public Works (MOPT), and carrying out
this decentralization process as efficiently as possible.
Objectives
2.          The basic aim of the study is to plan and design the process of
decentralizing the nationwide transportation infrastructure and define the
responsibility for the construction and maintenance functions, in line with
the Government's decentralization policies and the new constitutional
framework.  The specific objectives of the study are:
(a)   to determine what portion of the national highways network and the
associated physical, human and financial resources should be
transferred by the MOPT to the Departments;
(b)   to establish the necessary machinery to ensure that this transfer
proceeds smoothly over a transition period initially estimated at
three to five years, and that, once it has taken place, the
Departments can attain the desired level of efficiency.



- 153 -
ANNEX 7
Attachment 4
Page 2 of 5
Scoge of the studv
3.          The principal tasks to be performed by the consultants are the
following:
(a)   determine the optimum size of the national highways network, under
the jurisdiction of the MOPT, and the regional and departmental
road networks, under the jurisdiction of the Departments;
(b)   design a strategy for the phased redistribution of functions at
the national, regional and departmental levels for the
construction and maintenance of transportation infrastructure;
(C)   analyze the institutional capacity and resource availability in
the various Departments to perform the public works functions to
be assigned to them in the context of the decentralization
process;
(d)   establish criteria and proctdures for the transfer of human
resources (labor force) and physical resources (maintenance,
equipment and facilities) from the MOPT to the departmental
agencies;
(e)   establish criteria and procedures for the transfer of available
financial resources (tolls, taxes on gasoline and other charges)
from the central government to the departmental agencies, and for
mobilizing resources and obtaining loans at departmental and/or
regional level;
(f)   prepare guidelines for planning, budgeting and monitoring projects
in the public works and transportation sector in the Departments,
appropriately coordinated through the national and regional
organizations, and in accordance with the legal framework to be
established under the decentralization process; and
(g)   propose an Action Plan to govern the transfer of responsibilities
and resources to the Departments, establishing qualitative and
quantitative controls to determine the progress of this process
during the transition period.
4.          Determine the ootimum size of the national. recional and
DeDartmental road networks. The consultants will analyze the operational
(traffic) and functional characteristics of the highways forming the present
national road network (about 25,000 km) and the changes that can be expected
in the medium term as a result of the plans for economic liberalization
prepared by the Government, the location of production centers, expected
international traffic flows, etc. On the basis of this analysis, the
consultants will make proposals regarding: (i) the optimum size of the
principal trunk road network that should remain under national control,
specifying the highways concerned and the principal criteria for identifying



- 154 -
ANNEX 7
Attachment 4
Page 3 of 5
them; (ii) the list of roads recommended for transfer to the Departments,
indicating the current status of these roads (condition, resources to be
committed, works planned, etc.). In addition, the consultants will collect
information on the departmental road networks, and investment and maintenance
needs of the current departmental networks, and identify those roads that
require regional coordination.
5.          Desian a phased strategy for effective redistribution of oublic
works functions at the national. recional and Departmental level. The
consultants will formulate the criteria for distribution of the transportation
infrastructure construction and maintenance functions. To this end, the
consultants will analyze: (i) the legal framework and the roles to be
assigned to each level under the new regulations; (ii) current legislation and
the organizational structure of the responsible departmental agencies and
their links with other regional organizations; (iii) the policies required for
managing the downsizing and transfer of personnel and other resources in order
to minimize economic dislocations; and (iv) the desirability of employing
uniform criteria and standards for the design and execution of construction
and maintenance operations. In light of this analysis, the consultants will
design a strategy for the efficient, gradual decentralization, over a
transition period of three to five years, of the above-mentioned functions and
the transfer of roads and the associated human, physical and financial
resources from the central level to the departmental agencies.
6.          Analyze the departmental agencies' institutional canacitv.
resource availability and absorptive capacitv.  The consultants will prepare,
for all the Departments, an analysis of institutional capacity and the human,
physical (premises, maintenance, equipment, etc.), financial and
administrative resources available for performing their road construction and
maintenance, taking into account their expanded responsibilities under the
decentralization process. On the basis of this analysis, the consultants will
evaluate the departmental agencies' capacity to absorb new resources and will
identify the human, financial and administrative resources required to
strengthen their management capacity, proposing appropriate measures as
needed.
7.          Establish criteria and Procedures for the transfer of human and
ohvsical resources from the MOPT to the departmental agencies.  The
consultants will analyze the changes that will gradually occur in the MOPT's
operational needs during the decentralization process and will make
recommendations regarding the profile and size of the personnel structure and
the most suitable operating modalities for the new administrative structure.
In light of this study, and of the conclusions of the analysis on the future
needs and administrative capacity of the departmental agencies, the
consultants will identify the most appropriate mechanism to transfer the human
(labor force) and physical (maintenance, equipment and facilities) resources
from the MOPT to each of the departmental agencies.
8.          Establish criteria and orocedures for the transfer of available
financial resources and for mobilizing resources and obtainino loans at the

departmental (reqional) level. The consultants will analyze possible methods
of financing public works on the regional and departmental level through

The consultants will use tools already established by the National Planning

functions; therefore, the Action Plan will set out a timetable for integrating
each Department into the new system and the optimum schedule for the transfer
of functions to each Department during the transition period.

COLOMBIA
THIRD NATIONAL ROADS SECTOR PROJECT
outline of Terms of Reference for the Research Study of
the Behavior and Performance of Road Materials and Pavemento
Backoround
1.       MOPT started in 1984 a pavement research program directed at studying
the main local factors affecting pavement performance, particularly the effect
of Colombian road traffic conditions. The first phase of this research was
carried out through a one-year agreement with the University of Cauca.  It
selected 17 pavement sections from the road network; located throughout the
country, these test sections were representative of different pavement
structures, traffic and environmental conditions. Pavement evaluation studies
were conducted on such sections, including distress surveys, pavement
materials sampling and testing, Benkelman Beam deflections and traffic loads
weighing. Among other findings, the study led to defining truck factors which
are still in use for pavement design. In 1990, MOPT requested to the same
agency a second-phase program to follow up the research activities; the
resulting one-year program contributed to setting up modern testing devices
purchased by the University of Cauca and introducing some laboratory tests to
assess the basic properties of locally produced asphalt materials, in
coordination with ECOPETROL (Empresa Colombiana de Petroleo). The recently
set-up dynamic triaxial device is capable of measuring resilient and dynamic
modulus of road materials, which are related to basic performance criteria,
such as fatigue and deformation, and thus used by modern pavement design
methods. The proposed third phase of the pavement research program will apply
these methodologies to test actual and typical road materials obtained from
the existing pavement sections, and will study pavement performance through
periodical evaluations of those pavement sections. It will provide valuable
data to validate MOPT's standards for structural pavement design.
Obiectives
2.       The Study aims at upgrading the current knowledge on the behavior and
performance of road materials and pavements, through a better understanding of
the local conditions affecting pavement performance and a delineation of the
pavement deterioration patterns observed in typical pavements. The
implementation of the research findings will strengthen MOPT's capacity to
provide pavement designs tailored to local conditions, to schedule timely
maintenance and rehabilitation activities and to introduce more reliable
pavement technologies. The specific objectives of the study are:
a) to more effectively typify the behavior of road materials by using
modern laboratory testing techniques, and the effect of climatic



- 158 -
ANNEX 7
Attachment 5
Page 2 of 4
variables on pavement behavior by measuring environmental working
conditions prevailing in Colombian pavements;
b) to establish the deterioration patterns of standard pavement structures
under the typical service conditions observed in different regions of
the country and adjust performance models to predict such patterns; and
c) to organize additional research activities to validate the application
of conventional and non-conventional cost-effective solutions to improve
pavement performance.
Scope of the Study
3.       The research agency will review the data reported from the previous
research studies carried out in the country. The new research study will
comprise field tasks, mostly carried out in the 17 pavement test sections
identified in 1984, laboratory testing and analytical investigations, all of
them performed in close coordination with MOPT. The study will cover the
following five areas:
a) evaluating road materials behavior using modern laboratory testing
techniques;
b) studying the impact of environmental factors in pavement design and
performance;
c) monitoring pavement performance through periodic structural and
functional evaluation of the existing pavements in selected road
sections spread around the road network;
d) establishing tentative pavement deterioration curves for different
designs and environments; and
e) selecting experimental sections for trial of non-conventional cost-
effective solutions and validation of the research findings;
4.       Evaluatina road materials behavior usina modern laboratory testina
techniques. This phase will use the dynamic triaxial device which became
available through the previous research study, to analyze the properties of
typical road materials and to develop appropriate correlations with the
standard testing procedures traditionally used in Colombia. The study will
test materials samples obtained from the pavement test sections. In addition
to standard testing practices, the program will include: i) measuring dynamic
modulus of typical asphalt concrete mixes and establish fatigue performance
criteria; ii) measuring resilient modulus of subgrade soils and establish
permanent deformation criteria; and iii) analyzing the rheologic performance,
aging susceptibility of Colombian asphalt.
5.       Studvinc the imoact of environmental factors in pavement desian and
performance. The research study will analyze the effect of climate variables
on the behavior of selected pavement sections. Climatic data related to these
sections will be collected from the Colombian Institute of Meteorology and
compared to in-situ measurements of actual temperatures in asphalt layers,
water contents in unbound base and subbase courses, and equilibrium humidities



- 159 -
ANNEX 7
Attaohment E
Page 3 of 4
of subgrade soils. The atudy will identify the climatic variables showing
better correlation with pavement performance and will produce a climatic model
to infer such variables for every region of the country.
6.       Monitorina pavement performance throuah neriodic structural and
functional evaluation of the existina navements in selected road sections.
The study will follow up the performance evaluation of the selected pavement
sections begun in 1984. These sections, scattered throughout the different
regions of the country, will provide the field information to support the
research. The field work program will comprise: i) measuring pavement
deflections with Benkelman Beams and MOPT's Lacroix, and pavement roughness
with MOPT's APL; ii) surveying pavement distress; iii) measuring in-situ
properties of pavement layers; iv) sampling pavement materials to perform
laboratory testing; v) counting traffic volumes and weighing traffic loads;
and vi) collecting additional data needed to analyze pavement performanca
using available mechanistic-empiric performance models.
7.       Establishing tentative pavement deterioration curves for different
desians and environments. The research agency will analyze the data on
pavement performance reported by the periodical evaluation of the selected
pavement sections to establish deterioration curves related to typical
pavement structures and traffic and environmental conditions. These data will
be compared to pavement condition indicators predicted through the application
of the HDM-II and other well-known performance models to analyze the degree
of fitness of such models and to recommend the adjusting factors to more
closely reproduce local conditions.
S.       Selectina experimental sections for trial of non-conventional cost-
effective solutions and validation of research findings. Based on the
conclusions derived from the study, the research agency will propose non-
conventional cost-effective solutions to improve pavement performance. In
this context, it will select experimental sections for trial of such solutions
and outline the work program to be carried out, i._luding the tasks needed to
monitor their performance. The research agency will also assist MOPT in the
implementation of these trial sections, supervising the research work and
providing the necessary guidance to interpret the results.
Staffina
9.       The study will be carried out over a period of 36 months by a local
research agency. The selection of the research agency will be based on its
background on pavement research, availability of laboratory facilities and
specialized equipment, background of the proposed key personnel and experience
in similar studies. The key professional staff estimated for the study are:
i)   a pavement research specialist experienced in pavement rehabilitation,
laboratory testing, statistical analysis and research, who will be the
project leader (36 months);



- 160 -
ANNEX7
Attachment 5
Page 4 of 4
ii) a laboratory engineer specialized in road materials testing using modern
techniques (24 months);
iii) a pavement engineer experienced in pavement evaluation and data analysis
(24 months); and
iv) two high-skilled laboratory technicians experienced in routine
laboratory testing for soils, aggregates and asphalt materials, and
dosage and control of asphalt mixes (30 months).
Executing Aaency and Counterpart Staff
10.      The Technical Secretariat (TS) will supervise the study and will
implement its recommendations. TS will assign a coordinator to follow up work
progress and coordinate the research activities with the tasks being carried
out under the technical assistance in standards for structural pavement design
and road rehabilitation. MOPT will directly participate in monitoring
pavement performance by operating its Lacroix Deflectograph and APL inertial
profilometer. Special testing devices purchased for the study with Project
funds will be returned to MOPT's laboratory afterwards. In order to keep
operating the deflectograph and the inertial profilometer during the research
activities, the study will also finance the acquisition of the spare parts and
the cost of the repairs needed by such pieces of equipment.
Schedule and ReDorts
11.      The study will start in 1992, submitting the following reports:
a) quarterly reports on work progress, summarizing the tasks performed
during the period and assessing the adherence to the work program; and
b) a final report, summarizing the main findings and recommendations for
immediate application. The data collected by the study will be published
for future use. The research agency will furnish to MOPT a preliminary
version of this self-contained report 30 days before the end of the
contract and will issue the revised version, approved by MOPT, by the
contract's final date.

COLOMBIA
THIRD NATIONAL ROADS SECTOR PROJECT
Outline of Terms of Reference for a Study of the Road Construction Industry
Backaround
1.       The road construction industry has faced many difficulties in its
development path, despite the fact that it grew rapidly and now accounts for 3
percent of the GDP. The industry depends heavily on the Government's public
investment and availability of financing in reasonable terms. Other important
factors include availability of suitable insurance facilities, proper
legislation for contract administration and facilities to disseminate new
technologies.
Obiectives
2.       The objective of this study is to identify the main constraints and
obstacles preventing the domestic construction industry of Colombia from
assuming a more effective role in the country's construction and maintenance
programs and to develop appropriate detailed plans of action to overcome those
constraints.
3.       The work process should be to undertake a brief but balanced and
careful overview, and then to focus on the main issues on which action is
needed. Most of the effort of the study will, thus, be devoted to identifying
and considering alternative, viable solutions to the problems and to working
up action plans for their implementation.
4.       To ensure full commitment of the government and of the industry to
the execution of the strategy and action plans, they should be developed in
close collaboration with the Ministry of Public Works and Transports (MOPT),
acting liaison agency for the study team, and with the construction industry's
representatives and professional associations.
Scone of the Study
5.       The study of the construction industry in Colombia, and the
formulation of a strategy and action plans will be based on a careful
consideration of the following subjects: i) structure of the Industry; ii)
demand; iii) procurement and contract administration; iv) choice of
technology; v) the Industry's capacity; vi) financing; vii) legal aspects; and
viii) institutional aspects.
6.       Structure of the Industry

COLOMBIA
Third National Road Sector Proiect
Terms of Reference for a Study of Maintenance Dredgina
I.       INTRODUCTION
1.       The maintenance of the navigable channels in the River Magdalena and
the Canal del Dique requires the regular dredging of volumes that are
predictable within certain limits which are themselves determined primarily by
climatic variations. In earlier years river maintenance was contracted to the
Association of River Shipowners (ADENAVI), who undertook the task with their
own dredgers on the basis of an agreed three year budget, paid annually by the
MOPT. In 1980 rapidly rising costs and other problems caused a budgetry
crisis and the task, together with the ADENAVI dredgers, was transferred to
the MOPT. Since that date the work has been the responsibility of the
Division of Hydraulic Works (DOH) of the Directorate of River Transport and
Ports (DGNP). The DOH now has an aging fleet of nine dredgers with an average
age of 34 years; the newest dredger was purchased in 1976. The DOH has
approximately 467 personnel, most of whom work on, or in support of, the
dredgers and their related equipment.
2.       Despite the numerically large fleet, the performance record for the
maintenance dredging program has been poor, for a variety of reasons which
include:
a)   the age of the dredgers, lack of adequate supply of spare parts
and poor condition and non-availability of related equipment,
especially pipes;
b)   the intrinsic problems of maximizing performance in an
organization that is governed by public sector pay, conditions
and incentives; and
c)   the other demands made on the Division, chiefly for works
associated with the repair of river banks, in order to protect
riparian communities and roads. By their nature such demands
are unpredictable and present problems whose resolution has a
high priority.
3.       As a result, dredging costs are high and the results are inadequate,
so that river navigation has been interrupted and unreliable, with
consequential short term and longer term losses to river operators and to
river transport. The existence of the MOPT as the principal contractor of
dredging works, with its own fleet of dredgers, has inhibited the private
sector in the provision of alternative equipment. Nor, up to now, does there
appear to have been much demand for private dredging works, with the exception



- 169 -
ANNEX 7
Attachment 7
Page 2 of 6
of major works of seaport capital dredging, which require other equipment.
However, in the past few years the need for more reliable river dredging has
become so evident that a small number of private dredgers now exist and the
MOPT has made contracts with their owners, in order to supplement the
Ministry's own operations, either by direct hire or under an operating
contract.
4.        The other source of national dredging capacity is the National Port
Authority (COLPUERTOS), which owns one relatively new dredger and some older
ones. These dredgers work principally in the seaports of Barranquilla and
Buenaventura. There exists a law dating from 1984 to establish a national
dredging entity, EMCANALES, under mixed public and private sector ownership,
to undertake all public sector dredging, both river and seaports. However,
EMCANALES has not been established nor, under present policies of encouraging
maximum private sector participation in the seaport sector, and given the
imminent liquidation of COLPUERTOS, does this appear to be a likely event.
The study will review briefly the supply and demand aspects of the maritime
sector, in order to assess its potential impact on the recommendations made
for river dredging, without consideration of the institutional aspects for
meeting seaport dredging needs.
5.       The project components, for the improvement of the River Magdalena
between Barrancabermeja and La Gloria, and for the deferred maintenance
dredging in the Canal del Dique, put the problem of maintenance dredging into
high relief; clearly these two investments will be wasted if subsequent
reliable maintenance dredging cannot be achieved. The aim of the study is to
consider the institutional and contractual alternatives for the realization of
the required maintenance dredging in the river and the canal, and to make
appropriate recommendions.
II.      OBJECTIVE OF THE STUDY
S.       The objective of the study is to make recommendations that will
ensture the reliable and economical achievement of the maintenance dredging of
the River Magdalena between Barrancabermeja and La Gloria and of the Canal del
Dique, subsequent to the termination of the project works.
II1.     TASKS
7.       In the accomplishment of the above objective, the following tasks
will be undertaken:
Diaanosis
(1)      the historical dredging performance of the MOPT dredgers will be
assessed, based on data of works undertaken, location, volumes,
equipment allocated, performance achieved and unit costs, for the
period 1985 - 1990;



-- 170 -
ANNEX 7
Attachment 7
Page 3 of 6
(2)      in so far as the relevant data are available, a similar analysis will
be made for the final five years of the ADENAVI contract;
(3)      the above data will be compared with other data available from works
in Colombia and from international experience and general
observations made of any differences in overall performance
disclosed;
(4)      the annual dredging prcgrams of the MOPT will be compared with the
volumes achieved for the same period, any shortfalls identified, the
principal reasons examined and, from discussions with river operators
and from other sources, an estimate made of the economic consequences
of any such shortfalls;
Evaluation of SuDPlV
(5)      the MOPT dredgers and related equipment will be inspected and reports
made of their mechanical and structural condition. The reports will
include an assessment of any repairs and replacements necessary to
restore them to acceptable standards, with estimates of their cost
and of the expected performance, unit cost and reliability, were such
repairs to be done;
(6)      similar estimates of future performance will be made of private
sector and other non-MOPT Colombian dredgers;
(7)      an anlysis will be made of the human resources of the DOH, in terms
of their age, length of service, skills and experience and present
responsibilities;
Demand Analysis
(8)      on the basis of technical and historical data, estimates will be made
of the expected annual volumes of dredging, under the three
categories identified in paragraph 6 above, for the periods 1992-1994
(the years of project works) and thereafter up to the year 2000. The
estimates should be in terms of maximum, mininum and expected
volumes, on the basis of possible fluctuations in rainfall and other
variables. Any planned capital works should be identified and
quantified. A simple computer model should be developed, to assist
in the parametrization of the results, for purposes of sensitivity
analyses;
(9)      estimates will be made, though in less detailed terms, of the
expected volumes of dredging works for which the MOPT is not
responsible, for the same period;
Development of Alternatives



- 171 -
ANNEX 7
Attachment 7
Page 4 of 6
(10)     alternatives will be defined for the realization of the three
categories of works identified in task (8) above. The alternatives
should include the options of:
(a) force account, under which the MOPT does the work;
(b) delegated administration, under which the contractor supplies
labor and materials for the operation and maintenance of MOPT
equipment, working as directed;
(c) unit price, under which the contractor bids on the basis of a
unit price for different types of work, using the MOPT or his
own dredgers;
(d) standard contract for works (either individual works or by
sector), under which the contractor bids on the basis of lowest
unit cost, irrespectivb of the ownership of the equipment;
(e) for the maintenance of the channels that have been the subject
of the project: inclusion in the bidding for the project worksl
(f) such other alternatives as may appear, in the judgement of the
consultant, to merit consideration.
Analysis of Alternatives
(11)     the alternatives will be analysed in terms of their expected cost,
reliability in achievement, responsibility for cost overruns,
implications for the present MOPT equipment and personnel, and
administrative simplicity. Where alternatives have significant
differences in reliability, risk analysis will be used in order to
quantify the impact of such differences. The analysis will be done
in economic terms and in financial terms, from the point of view of
the MOPT.
Recommendation and Action Plan
(12)     the consultants will recommend the alternative that in their
judgement best achieves the objective defined in paragraph 6 above,
with its expected cost and other implications. The steps required
for the implementation of the recommended strategy shall be
identified and presented as an Action Plan, identifying cost, timing
adid responsibilities.

V.       EXECUTING AGENCY AND COUNTERPART
10.      The executing agency will be the MOPT, in close coordination with the
National Planning Department (DNP). Responsibility for the execution of the
study within the MOPT will be with the Planning Division, who will be assisted
in their work by a steering group including the Director of Infrastructure
(DNP), the Director of River Navigation (MOPT) and the Technical Director of
the Superintendencia of Ports (MOPT).
11.        Counterpart personnel will be provided by the Directorate of River
Transport and by the Planning Division.
VI.      PROGRAM AND REPORTS
12.      The outline work program is defined by the reports that have to be
submitted at the end of each month. These are:
end of month 1: - Historical Performance (tasks 1 - 4)
- Assessment of Resources (tasks 5 - 7)
- Estimates of Demand (tasks 8 & 9)
end of month 2: - Definition of Alternatives (task 10)
and final version of the earlier reports.
end of month 3: - Analysis of Alternatives (task 11)
- Recommendation (draft: task 12, without Action
Plan) and final version of report "Definition of
Alternatives".
end of month 4: - Final Report and Action Plan.
13.      Thus the government counterpart will have the first two weeks of
month 2, to consider the draft reports on Historical Performance, Assessment
of Resources and Estimates of Demand, the first two weeks of month 3 to
consider the draft report on Alternatives and the first two weeks of month 4

to consider the draft Analysis of Alternatives and Recommendation. The Final
Report will thus include six chapters, corresponding to the earlier draft
reports, all of which will have been reviewed by the Counterpart, plus the
Action Plan.

COLOMBIA
THIRD NATIONAL ROADS SECTOR PROJECT
Trainino Component
1. Elackagrund
1.01     Several attempts have been made in the past to establish a sound
training program through previous Bank projects, with varying intensity and
success. In the early 80s, MOPT hired a foreign consulting firm for technical
assistance in road maintenance management. The consultants put in place a
training program to improve technlcal and managerial skills of MOPT staff
involved in road and equLpment maintenance, but as this program was highly
dependant on consultants' work, it was interrupted once the technical
assistance finished its services in 1982. After that, in 1984, MOPT made an
agreement with SENAY to design and carry out a new training program,
focusing mainly on equLpment maintenance and repair, and on managerial
development in other areas of MOPT activities besides road maintenance. Under
this agreement, since 1984, about 1500 mechanics have been successfully
trained through basic and productive courses combining theory, practice and
on-the-job training, and 8 mechanics have been fully trained as instructors
for these productive courses. Also, some seminars were held from 1985 to 1986
in order to improve managerial skills at high management levels but with
little impact in the long run due to high staff mobLlity.  Additionally, in
1986, SENA conducted a diagnosis of MOPT organization finding that about 50%
of district personnel were reaching their retirement age and that more
training was needed to overcome operational difficulties. In 1989 MOPT
renewed its agreement with SENA, including the training of eight selected
heavy equipment operators as equipment instructors; it is expected that this
task will be completed by the end of 1991.
1.02     The Directorate of Industrial Relations (DIR) has been responsible
for the preparation and implementation of this training program since 1984.
The need of technical cooperation to improve the training capabilities within
this directorate was envisaged during the preparation of Loans 2121-CO and
2829-CO. Provisions in Loan 2829-CO included engaging local consultants for
about 48 staff-months to advise DIR in planning, organizing and executing
training programs as well as foreign consultants (60 staff-months) to organize
I/ SENA (Servicio Nacional de AXrendizaie) is the main government agency
dedicated to manpower training. According to local laws, it receives a levy
equivalent to 0.5% of MOPT's personnel budget. The agreement between MOPT and
SENA defines the kind of services the latter will give, but no direct payment
is involved.



- 175 -
Page 2 of 10
a training program for instructors, supervisors, and heavy machines operators
and maintenance personnel. In 1986 MOPT requested technical assistance from
ICICOM (Instituto de Canacitacion de la Industria de la Construccion Mexicana)
to organize and implement a continuous training program directed to improving
MOPT equipment operators' skills; however, no agreement was finally achieved,
in part due to the high cost of the ICICOM proposal. Neither ICICOM
specialist nor local or foreign consultants were hired.
1.03     From 1984 to 1989, MOPT entered into four annual contracts with the
University of Cauca for the support of two Msc. Courses in Transport and Road
Engineering. Through this arrangement up to 25 MOPT professlonals attended
either the whole one-year program or speciflc courses of two weeks duration.
In 1988 MOPT contracted with the same institutlon the organizatlon of 10
seminars; to date, seven seminars have been held in the areas of flexible
pavement technology, upgrading the skilLs of about 100 MOP? offlcials. These
events were financed by MOPT's own budget.
2. The Proiect's Traininer Comnonent Obiectives and Descriotion.
A. Oblectives.
2.01     The major objectives of the project's tralning program are to:
a) strengthen the performance capabillties of MOPT personnel in the areas
of: i) road maintenance; Li) heavy equlpment operation; iii) heavy
equipment maintenance; iv) road planning and financing; v) read design,
construction and supervision; vi) bridge design and construction; vii)
project environmental evaluation and control; viii) navigation and
ports; ix) intermodal transport facilitation; and x) computer
technology, administration and clerical skills.
b) develop the staff skills needed to ensure full implementation of the
new procedures introduced in MOPT operations through the technical
assistance and studies described in Annex 7, in the areas of highway
maintenance management, standards for pavement structural design and
road rehabilitation, supervision of road works and slope stabilit:
problems;
c) disseminate among consultants and contractors the new standards for
road design and construction introduced in MOPT operations, such as
technical specifications, standards for road geometric design and
guLdelines for the preparation of flnal engineering studies, to
f&cilitate a full and smooth lntegration of such standards; and
d) strengthen the Directorate of Industrial Relatlons within MOPT to plan,
organize, coordinate, implement, and evaluate relevant tralnlng
programs.

S. Descriotion of the Training Proqram.
2.02     The training program would comprise four main areas: i) a series of
training courses in Colombia for MOPT staff, consultants and contractors; Ii)
on-the-job training provided by the technical assistance program outlined in
Annex 7; iii) study tours, courses and internships abroad for senior level
officials; and iv) technical assistance and internships abroad for MOPT
instructors and senior level officials within the Directorate of Industrial
Relations.
a) Training Courses. The Department of Industrial Relations (DIR) will
conduct 715 local courses and seminars in the ten subject areas
mentioned in para. 2.01. The training program is expected to involve
about 6900 * MOPT officials and 1000 consultants, microempresas, large
contractors personnel and transport operators. Sources to organize and
perform these courses in Colombia would include: 16 MOPT instructors; 7
foreign consultants hired under the technical assistance component;
local and expatriate experts hired for course delivery; and external
training institutions, such as SENA, the University of Cauca,
specialized equipment supplier firms and international agencies, like
the Pan-American Institute of Highways.  However, in all cases, course
contents would be approved by DIR (see para. 3.02). The tentative
series of courses, grouped into the ten subject areas, is shown in
Attachment 1. The program focus mainly on developing practical and
relevant skills, needed to carry out MOPT's policies and activities.
Therefore, training methods vary according to training objectives and
target group.
b)  On-the-job training.  The technical assistance program outlined in Annex
7 will provide on-the-job train:ng to MOPT staff. The counterpart
personnel assigned by MOPT will actively participate In all technical
assistance activities to ensure full knowledge of procedures and systems
developed by consultants. Additionally, specific short training courses
have been outlined in Attachment 1 to spread cut among other MOPT staff
the necessary skillg to operate these systems. Short classroom
instruction and exercises followed by post-course performance evaluation
and in-service guidance would be provided both in Bogota and in the
districts. The consultants engaged through these technical assistance
activities will be responsible not only for preparing and delivering
such courses but for training MOPT counterpart staff to deliver them in
the future, once the consultant's services are completed. DIR will
participate in this process and w'il check that the training objectives
are achieved.
c)  Study to2rs. courses  seminars, conferences. and internships abroad.
During project preparation, a preliminary list of international courses,
seminars and conferences related to MOPT's priorities was identified.
It is expected that 94 MOPT senior professional and management staff
will attend these events during the project and will be exposed to



- 177 -
ANNEX 8
Page 4 of 10
technological development in other countries. Through an agreement with
the Pan American Institute of Highways, soma courses organized by the
FHWA will be followed by short job assignments in selected agencies,
providing hands-on application of the technology received. About 31
staff-month are anticipated to provide for internships of one to three-
months duration. These internships are intended for staff with more
than two years work with MOPT and at least one year in the field related
to the fellowship; beneficiaries' commitment to working at least one
year within MOPT after returning will also be required, according to
TORs prepared by DIR. The scope of this component is also summarized in
Attachment 1. Participants would have to prepare a back-to-office
report summarizing the most relevant findings and recommendations and
their potential application to BIOPT work.
d) Technical assistance and internehins abroad for DIR. A key element in
th's training program is the improvement in MOPT in-house capability to
provide efficient training activities. In addition to the consultants
and instructors required for the execution of the training program
described above, consultants would be engaged to help DIR in the
development and delivery of courses and seminars, and in the
coordination of all of the training components. It is envisaged that
this task would require the full time work of one local training
consultant during the first year of the program and about two
specialist-month per year of a foreign training adviser. Outlines of
the terms of reference for this technical assistance are included in
Attachment 2. The project would also provide training abroad (study
tours and internships) for five DIR high level staff and 16 MOPT
instructors in mechanics and heavy equipment operation.
2.03     The details of the training program are shown in the following table,

at about 7900 persons, involving MOPT officials trained botlh locally and

personnel. In agreement with the Government's decentralization policy, the
training program will be also opened to staff from the Secretariats of Public
Works of the departments (SPWs). An increasing number of vacancies will
become available for SPWs key staff during 1994-95; participating staff will
be selected from a list of candidates periodically proposed by the SPWs.
